PROLOGAI COMPLETION v66 -> v67: RUVECTOR SHADOW STORE AND REBUILD

Release summary: backend_ruvector extended with an in-process shadow store
(vbr_shadow/5) and a rebuild predicate (vbr_rebuild/1) to mitigate data loss
when the RuVector server is restarted.  vb_rebuild/1 wired into vector_backend
as a backend-agnostic interface predicate.

Delivered artifacts:

packs/vector_backend/prolog/backend_ruvector.pl  (updated)
   Dynamic fact:    vbr_shadow/5 — mirrors every insert; survives server restart
   New predicate:   vbr_insert_http/5 — raw HTTP PUT (no shadow); used by rebuild
   Updated:         vbr_insert/4 — now also records to vbr_shadow/5
   Updated:         vbr_delete/2 — now removes shadow entry (was full no-op)
   Updated:         vbr_close/1 — now clears all shadows for the collection
   New export:      vbr_rebuild/1 — rebuild index from shadow after server restart
   New export:      vbr_shadow_count/2 — diagnostic count of shadow entries

packs/vector_backend/prolog/vector_backend.pl  (updated)
   New export:      vb_rebuild/1 — backend-agnostic rebuild interface
   New predicate:   vb_dispatch_rebuild/2 (prolog: no-op; ruvector: vbr_rebuild)

packs/vector_backend/test/test_backend_ruvector.pl  (updated)
   Added:           AC-RV-008 through AC-RV-012 (five new tests)
   Total tests:     12 (all passing)

Rebuild usage:
   After a RuVector server restart, restore the index with:
       ?- vb_rebuild(Ref).
   or equivalently:
       ?- vbr_rebuild(rv_ref(CollName, BaseUrl)).

Shadow store lifecycle:
   vbr_insert/4  -> assertz(vbr_shadow/5)       [adds]
   vbr_delete/2  -> retractall(vbr_shadow/5)    [removes one Id]
   vbr_close/1   -> retractall(vbr_shadow/5)    [removes all for collection]
   vbr_rebuild/1 -> reads vbr_shadow/5, does NOT modify it

Limitations (deferred):
   - Shadow store lives in the SWI-Prolog process; a Prolog restart also clears
     shadows.  Full durability requires persisting shadows to disk (future work).
   - Silent insert failure (Risk 2): if the HTTP PUT fails due to server error,
     the shadow is still recorded; the index and shadow diverge.  A health-check
     predicate with automatic rebuild is planned for a future release.
   - vbr_delete/2 removes the shadow but the server-side HNSW index still retains
     the vector (no per-point DELETE endpoint).  Ghost results remain until the
     next full rebuild (vbr_rebuild/1) is called.

SPARC documentation: Refinement v63 -> v64, Completion v66 -> v67 (this release).
README updated. Tutorial updated. Scientific paper updated.

Score improvement: none (durability and reliability improvement).

WORK PACKAGE 80: INDUCTION PACK

Pack: induction
Layer: 59
Prefix: id_
Branch: feature/pr80-induction-pack

Purpose:
Provides grid-pair inductive primitives for reasoning about what changed
between an input and output grid: color substitution maps, recolor
detection, uniform output detection, size ratio and integer scale
detection, and per-cell change analysis.

Predicates (14):
  id_grid_dims/3          - dimensions of a grid
  id_input_colors/2       - sorted distinct colors in input
  id_output_colors/2      - sorted distinct colors in output
  id_new_colors/3         - colors in output not in input
  id_lost_colors/3        - colors in input not in output
  id_changed_cells/3      - cells that changed value
  id_unchanged_cells/3    - cells that kept their value
  id_color_map/3          - inferred Old-New color substitution pairs
  id_is_recolor/2         - true when output is consistent color substitution
  id_uniform_output/2     - true when all output cells share one color
  id_output_color/2       - single uniform output color (fails if non-uniform)
  id_size_ratio/3         - ratio of output dims to input dims
  id_is_scale/2           - true when output is an integer scale of input
  id_scale_factor/3       - integer scale factor

Deliverables:
  packs/induction/pack.pl - pack descriptor
  packs/induction/prolog/induction.pl - 14 id_* predicates

WORK PACKAGE 81: GRAVITY PACK

Pack: gravity
Layer: 60
Prefix: gv_
Branch: feature/pr81-gravity-pack

Purpose:
Provides gravity and settling operations on grids. Non-background cells
can be made to fall in any of four directions (down, up, left, right).
Specific colors can be singled out to fall through background cells
while treating other non-background cells as obstacles.

Predicates (14):
  gv_col_values/3    - extract column values as a list
  gv_set_col/4       - replace a column in a grid
  gv_compact_col/3   - all non-BG values sink to column bottoms
  gv_compact_row/3   - all non-BG values shift to row lefts
  gv_fall_down/3     - non-BG cells fall to bottom of each column
  gv_fall_up/3       - non-BG cells rise to top of each column
  gv_fall_left/3     - non-BG cells shift to left of each row
  gv_fall_right/3    - non-BG cells shift to right of each row
  gv_settle_color/4  - specific color falls to bottom past BG
  gv_float_color/4   - specific color rises to top past BG
  gv_stack_down/4    - alias for gv_settle_color
  gv_stack_up/4      - alias for gv_float_color
  gv_apply_col/4     - apply custom transform to each column
  gv_apply_row/4     - apply custom transform to each row

Deliverables:
  packs/gravity/pack.pl - pack descriptor
  packs/gravity/prolog/gravity.pl - 14 gv_* predicates
  packs/gravity/test/test_gravity.pl - 29 PLUnit tests (29/29 pass)

WORK PACKAGE 82: NOISE PACK

Pack: noise
Layer: 61
Prefix: ns_
Branch: feature/pr82-noise-pack

Purpose:
Provides binary mask operations and noise/density analysis on grids.
Binary masks are grids of 0s and 1s used to select, exclude, or
replace cells. Noise analysis identifies and removes cells that
deviate from the dominant color in a grid. Color isolation and
sparse/dense classification support the common pattern of identifying
outliers in a predominantly uniform grid.

Predicates (14):
  ns_mask_apply/4      - apply binary mask with fill color
  ns_mask_invert/3     - flip all mask bits (0<->1)
  ns_mask_and/3        - pointwise AND of two masks
  ns_mask_or/3         - pointwise OR of two masks
  ns_mask_from_color/3 - build mask: 1 where grid has color
  ns_mask_to_region/2  - mask to r(R,C) region list
  ns_region_to_mask/4  - region list to mask grid
  ns_noise_cells/3     - cells differing from majority color
  ns_denoise/3         - replace noise with majority color
  ns_majority_color/2  - most frequent color in grid
  ns_color_count/3     - count occurrences of a color
  ns_sparse_cells/3    - cells with rarely-occurring color (< N times)
  ns_dense_cells/3     - cells with frequently-occurring color (>= N times)
  ns_isolate_color/3   - keep one color, zero out everything else

Deliverables:
  packs/noise/pack.pl - pack descriptor
  packs/noise/prolog/noise.pl - 14 ns_* predicates
  packs/noise/test/test_noise.pl - 33 PLUnit tests (33/33 pass)

WORK PACKAGE 83: GENERATE PACK

Pack: generate
Layer: 62
Prefix: ge_
Branch: feature/pr83-generate-pack

Purpose:
Provides predicates for constructing new grids from scratch using
common visual patterns: uniform fill, horizontal and vertical
gradients, checkerboard, horizontal and vertical stripes, bordered
rectangles, diagonal and anti-diagonal lines, frame rings, crosses,
identity matrices, cell-color maps, and pattern tiling.

Predicates (14):
  ge_uniform/4          - uniform color fill
  ge_gradient_h/4       - horizontal gradient (column C -> C mod NColors)
  ge_gradient_v/4       - vertical gradient (row R -> R mod NColors)
  ge_checkerboard/5     - alternating two colors by (R+C) mod 2
  ge_stripes_h/4        - horizontal color stripes cycling a list
  ge_stripes_v/4        - vertical color stripes cycling a list
  ge_border_rect/5      - outermost ring one color, interior another
  ge_diagonal/4         - main diagonal cells colored, rest zero
  ge_antidiagonal/4     - anti-diagonal cells colored, rest zero
  ge_frame/5            - outermost ring one color, interior BG
  ge_cross/5            - middle row and column colored, rest BG
  ge_identity_grid/3    - N x N identity: diagonal=One, rest=0
  ge_from_map/3         - build from a list of r(R,C)-Color pairs
  ge_repeat_pattern/4   - tile a pattern grid to fill Rows x Cols

  lk_delete/3           - remove a key-value pair
  lk_map_values/3       - transform all values in a map
  lk_from_pairs/2       - build a map from Key-Value pairs
  lk_grid_row/3         - row lookup in a grid
  lk_grid_col/3         - column lookup in a grid
  lk_grid_cell/4        - cell lookup by (R,C)
  lk_color_positions/3  - Color to positions index map
  lk_position_color/3   - position to Color index map
  lk_invert/2           - invert association list keys and values

  cc_largest8/3         - largest 8-connected component
  cc_smallest4/3        - smallest 4-connected component
  cc_border_cells/3     - border cells of a region
  cc_interior_cells/3   - interior cells of a region

  mo_boundary8/3      - 8-connected boundary cells
  mo_ring4/4          - 4-connected outward ring
  mo_fill_holes4/4    - fill enclosed background holes

   of the output argument, breaking unification in callers. Fixed by removing
   these declarations (outputs are not goal arguments).
3. meta_predicate on internal helpers (hy_score_pair_, hy_rank_one_) caused
   context confusion in maplist calls. Fixed by removing from internal helpers.
4. hy_describe had choicepoints because the catch-all third clause matched
   after the first two. Fixed by adding cuts to the first two clauses.

SPARC docs updated:
  PrologAI_1_Specification_v60.txt - Part 85 added
  PrologAI_2_Pseudocode_v53.txt - Part 85 added
  PrologAI_3_Architecture_v54.txt - ARCH-61 added
  PrologAI_4_Refinement_v108.txt - AC-HY-001..030 added
  PrologAI_5_Completion_v111.txt - this entry

WORK PACKAGE 116 - GRAVITY PACK

Name: gravity
Layer: 95
Prefix: gv_
Branch: feature/pr116-gravity-pack
Status: COMPLETE

Predicates (14):
  gv_pack_row_left/3    - compact non-Bg values to the left in a row
  gv_pack_row_right/3   - compact non-Bg values to the right in a row
  gv_pack_col_up/3      - compact non-Bg values to the top in a column list
  gv_pack_col_down/3    - compact non-Bg values to the bottom in a column list
  gv_fall_left/3        - all non-Bg cells slide left per row
  gv_fall_right/3       - all non-Bg cells slide right per row
  gv_fall_down/3        - all non-Bg cells fall downward per column
  gv_fall_up/3          - all non-Bg cells rise upward per column
  gv_fall_dir/4         - dispatch gravity by direction atom (down/up/left/right)
  gv_fall_color_left/4  - only Color slides left; other non-Bg cells are walls
  gv_fall_color_right/4 - only Color slides right; other non-Bg cells are walls
  gv_fall_color_down/4  - only Color falls down; other non-Bg cells are walls
  gv_fall_color_up/4    - only Color rises up; other non-Bg cells are walls
  gv_fall_color_dir/5   - dispatch color-specific gravity by direction atom

Description:
The cluster pack (Layer 102) provides 14 predicates for spatial proximity and

  cl_center/3             - integer centroid (round of mean row and col)
  cl_diameter/2           - maximum pairwise Chebyshev distance in a set
  cl_spread/3             - bounding box dimensions (row span, col span)
  cl_group_by_color/4     - group cells by their grid color; parallel Colors and Groups lists
  cl_sort_by_dist/4       - sort cells by ascending Chebyshev distance to a point
  cl_nearest_pair/3       - pair of cells with minimum pairwise Chebyshev distance
  cl_farthest_pair/3      - pair of cells with maximum pairwise Chebyshev distance
  cl_cells_in_band/6      - filter cells within a row-column band

WORK PACKAGE 127: ENCLOSURE PACK (en_* prefix, Layer 106)
Date: 2026-06-25
Branch: feature/pr127-enclosure-pack

Purpose:
The enclosure pack (Layer 106) provides 14 deterministic predicates for
classifying background cells in 2D grids as exterior (reachable from the
grid border) or interior (enclosed by non-background walls), decomposing
color regions into boundary and interior subsets, and testing various forms
of spatial surround.

Predicates:
  en_border_cells/2     - all cells on the four grid edges
  en_outer_cells/3      - all Bg cells reachable from the border (exterior)
  en_inner_cells/3      - all Bg cells not reachable from the border (interior)
  en_is_inner/4         - test if a cell is an enclosed Bg cell
  en_is_outer/4         - test if a cell is an exterior Bg cell
  en_fill_inner/4       - paint all enclosed Bg cells with a given color
  en_inner_count/3      - count enclosed Bg cells
  en_has_inner/2        - test if any enclosed Bg cell exists
  en_inner_components/3 - connected components of enclosed Bg cells
  en_outer_components/3 - connected components of exterior Bg cells
  en_fill_hole/6        - fill one enclosed Bg component at a given cell
  en_boundary_cells/3   - Color cells on the boundary of a Color region
  en_interior_cells/3   - Color cells strictly interior to a Color region
  en_is_surrounded/4    - test if all orthogonal neighbors are a given color

Key algorithms:
  Outer/inner classification: BFS from all border Bg cells (en_bfs_bg_).
  Reached cells are exterior; unreached Bg cells (set difference via
  subtract/3) are interior. Deterministic and correct for any simply or
  multiply connected region topology.

  Connected components: en_comp_bfs_ performs BFS within a given available
  cell set; the accumulated visited list is the component. en_all_comps_
  iterates subtract/3 to partition the cell set into components without
  repeated work.

  Boundary/interior: include/3 with YALL lambdas. Free variables in lambda
  bodies are fresh for each invocation due to YALL's copy_term semantics.
  memberchk/2 is used instead of member/2 in en_is_inner, en_is_outer,
  and en_fill_hole to prevent residual choicepoints on deterministic lookups.

Tests:
  42 PLUnit acceptance tests pass (3 per predicate), verifying the primary
  case, an edge case, and a boundary condition for each predicate. All
  tests pass with no choicepoint warnings.

Documentation:
  docs/PrologAI_1_Specification_v92.txt      - Part 117: EN-EN-001 through EN-EN-014
  docs/PrologAI_2_Pseudocode_v85.txt         - Part 117 pseudocode
  docs/PrologAI_3_Architecture_v86.txt       - PART ARCH-93
  docs/PrologAI_4_Refinement_v140.txt        - Part 117: AC-EN-001 through AC-EN-042
  docs/PrologAI_5_Completion_v143.txt        - Work Package 127 (this entry)
  docs/tutorial/Ch88_Enclosure.txt           - tutorial chapter
  README.md                                  - pack count updated to 125

Mentova: Acc_147 (paper + announcement)

END OF WORK PACKAGE 127


WORK PACKAGE 128 - HULL PACK

Layer: 107
Module: hull
Prefix: hu_
Feature branch: feature/pr128-hull-pack
Date: 2026-06-25

Summary:
  Work Package 128 adds the hull pack, a Layer 107 symbolic reasoning
  module providing 14 predicates for convex hull computation and polygon
  geometry on 2D integer-coordinate cell sets. The pack implements Andrew's
  monotone chain algorithm, adapted for grid (R-down, C-right) coordinates,
  and provides derived operations: area, perimeter, containment testing,
  concavity extraction, filling, diameter computation, aspect measurement,
  rectangle testing, and centroid estimation.

Predicates (14, hu_* prefix):
  hu_convex_hull/2      - Andrew's monotone chain; CW screen-order hull
  hu_is_convex/1        - discrete convexity: shape equals hull interior
  hu_hull_size/2        - count of hull vertices (excluding collinear points)
  hu_hull_area2/2       - twice hull area (integer shoelace formula)
  hu_in_hull/3          - point inside/on convex hull (edge cross product test)
  hu_cells_in_hull/3    - all grid cells inside hull
  hu_fill_hull/4        - paint hull interior with a color
  hu_concavities/4      - Bg cells in hull but absent from the shape
  hu_diameter/4         - farthest pair of cells (max squared distance)
  hu_aspect/3           - bounding box height and width of the hull
  hu_is_rect/1          - 4-vertex hull with all right angles
  hu_hull_perim2/2      - sum of squared hull edge lengths
  hu_centroid/3         - floor of average row/col of hull vertices
  hu_hull_contains/2    - test if all SubCells are inside the hull

Key implementation notes:
  Andrew's monotone chain algorithm: sort by (C, R), build lower half-hull
  (left-to-right) and upper half-hull (right-to-left) by trimming points
  that cause non-clockwise turns (cross product Z >= 0). The trim condition
  Z >= 0 corresponds to standard algorithm's pop-when-Z<=0 in y-up Cartesian,
  inverted because screen R increases downward. Result is a CW hull.

  Point-in-hull test: for CW hull, inside iff all edge cross products Z =< 0.
  Degenerate 2-vertex hull uses collinearity + bounding-box bounds.

  Imports: library(lists) for member/2, nth0/3, append/3, reverse/2,
  min_list/2, max_list/2, last/2; library(apply) for maplist/3.

Tests:
  42 PLUnit acceptance tests pass (3 per predicate), verifying the primary
  case, an edge case, and a boundary/failure condition for each predicate.
  All tests pass with no choicepoint warnings.

Documentation:
  docs/PrologAI_1_Specification_v93.txt      - Part 118: HU-HU-001 through HU-HU-014
  docs/PrologAI_2_Pseudocode_v86.txt         - Part 118 pseudocode
  docs/PrologAI_3_Architecture_v87.txt       - PART ARCH-94
  docs/PrologAI_4_Refinement_v141.txt        - Part 118: AC-HU-001 through AC-HU-042
  docs/PrologAI_5_Completion_v144.txt        - Work Package 128 (this entry)
  docs/tutorial/Ch89_Hull.txt               - tutorial chapter
  README.md                                  - pack count updated to 126

Mentova: Acc_148 (paper + announcement)

END OF WORK PACKAGE 128


WORK PACKAGE 129: PATCH PACK (Layer 108)

Pack: patch
Prefix: pa_
Layer: 108
Branch: feature/pr129-run-pack
Predicates: 14
Tests: 42 (all pass)

Description:
  Sub-grid extraction and template matching for integer-valued grids.
  A patch is a rectangular sub-grid (list of lists of integers).

Predicates:
  pa_extract/6       - extract an H x W rectangular sub-patch at (R0, C0)
  pa_dims/3          - get patch height and width
  pa_match/4         - non-deterministically find where a patch occurs
  pa_match_all/3     - all matching positions as a list
  pa_match_count/3   - count of matching positions
  pa_match_bg/4      - match with background wildcard cells
  pa_slides/4        - enumerate all H x W sub-patches with positions
  pa_unique_patches/4 - sorted list of distinct patches
  pa_most_common_patch/5 - most frequently occurring patch and count
  pa_diff/3          - cells where two same-size patches differ
  pa_is_uniform/2    - test if all cells have the same color
  pa_flip_h/2        - horizontal (left-right) flip
  pa_flip_v/2        - vertical (top-bottom) flip
  pa_rot90/2         - 90-degree clockwise rotation

Algorithm Notes:
  Template matching: pa_match enumerates all candidate top-left corners and
  uses Prolog structural unification against the extracted sub-patch.
  Background wildcard matching: pa_match_bg applies a cell-level test where
  Bg cells in the pattern are treated as "don't care" wildcards.
  Rotation: CW formula Rotated(r', c') = Patch(H-1-c', r'); output is W x H.
  Most-common: msort preserves duplicates; pa_count_groups_ identifies runs.

Imports: library(lists) for member/2, nth0/3, append/3, reverse/2, last/2;
  library(apply) for maplist/3.

Tests:
  42 PLUnit acceptance tests pass (3 per predicate), no choicepoint warnings.

Documentation:
  docs/PrologAI_1_Specification_v94.txt      - Part 119: PA-PA-001 through PA-PA-014
  docs/PrologAI_2_Pseudocode_v87.txt         - Part 119 pseudocode
  docs/PrologAI_3_Architecture_v88.txt       - PART ARCH-95
  docs/PrologAI_4_Refinement_v142.txt        - Part 119: AC-PA-001 through AC-PA-042
  docs/PrologAI_5_Completion_v145.txt        - Work Package 129 (this entry)
  docs/tutorial/Ch90_Patch.txt              - tutorial chapter
  README.md                                  - pack count updated to 127

  nm_count_prefix_/4 clause 1 (empty list base case) required a cut (!)
  to prevent the catch-all clause 3 from matching an empty list.

  causing nm_row_modes and nm_filter4/8 to collect each value twice.

WP 163 RELEASE RECORD: INDEX PACK (ix_* prefix, Layer 142)

Date: 2026-06-25
Branch: feature/wp163-index
Pack: packs/index/
Predicates: 14 (ix_row_grid, ix_col_grid, ix_sum_grid, ix_diff_grid,
             ix_prod_grid, ix_manhattan_grid, ix_chebyshev_grid, ix_mod_grid,
             ix_row_mod_grid, ix_col_mod_grid, ix_mask_rows, ix_mask_cols,
             ix_apply, ix_from)
Tests: 42/42 pass
SPARC: Spec v128, Pseudo v121, Arch v122, Refinement v176, Completion v179
Mentova: Acc_183

Summary: The index pack generates coordinate-valued 2D grids for use as
operands in arithmetic and masking operations. It fills the gap between
individual-cell coordinate access (available through grid pack primitives)
and full grid-level coordinate field operations. Coordinate grids created
by ix_row_grid, ix_col_grid, ix_sum_grid, ix_diff_grid, ix_prod_grid,
ix_manhattan_grid, and ix_chebyshev_grid can be combined with value grids
using ix_apply (add, sub, mul, max_op, min_op) to produce transformed grids.
Modular variants (ix_mod_grid, ix_row_mod_grid, ix_col_mod_grid) create
repeating stripe patterns. ix_mask_rows and ix_mask_cols select arbitrary
rows or columns by index list. ix_from creates signed linear offsets from
a reference point using row-major stride.

END OF WP 163 RELEASE RECORD

    fd_fold_both/5.

Tests: 42 PLUnit tests, all passing.

Symmetry convention: fd_sym_h and fd_sym_v use the between-rows mirror formula
(2R+1-I and 2C+1-J). This is consistent with fd_fold_h and fd_fold_v: the fold
crease sits between rows/cols R and R+1. The formula avoids the vacuous symmetry
at R=0 that arises with the center-row formula (2R-I).

WP 166 RELEASE RECORD

Work Package: 166
Pack name: warp
Prefix: wr_
Layer: 145
Module file: packs/warp/prolog/warp.pl
Pack manifest: packs/warp/pack.pl
Test file: packs/warp/test/test_warp.pl

Release date: 2026-06-26

Summary: The warp pack provides 14 predicates for shear transformations, cyclic
(toroidal) shifts, per-row arbitrary offset warping, anti-diagonal transposition,
and detection of shear relationships between grids. The central capability is the
horizontal shear (wr_shear_h), where row I shifts right by I*Step, and its vertical
counterpart (wr_shear_v), where column J shifts down by J*Step. Cyclic variants
(wr_cyclic_shear_h, wr_cyclic_shear_v) wrap around toroidally with no fill color
needed. The anti-diagonal transpose (wr_transpose_anti) maps (R,C) to (W-1-C, H-1-R)
and is an involution on square grids. Detection predicates (wr_find_shear_h,
wr_find_shear_v) search a bounded step range for the shear that maps one grid to
another.

Test results: 42/42 PLUnit tests pass.

SPARC documentation updates in this release:

    Pseudocode v124: Part 156, pseudocode for all 14 predicates.

WP 167 RELEASE RECORD

Work Package: 167
Pack name: border
Prefix: br_
Layer: 146
Module file: packs/border/prolog/border.pl
Pack manifest: packs/border/pack.pl
Test file: packs/border/test/test_border.pl

Release date: 2026-06-26

Summary: The border pack provides 14 predicates for concentric ring analysis of 2D
grids. The central concept is the ring depth formula: ring_depth(R,C) = min(R, H-1-R,
C, W-1-C). Ring 0 is the outermost border ring; ring N is N steps inward from the outer
edge. The maximum ring index is (min(H,W)-1)//2. Predicates cover ring cell enumeration
(br_ring_cells), value extraction (br_ring_vals), uniformity testing (br_ring_color,
br_is_uniform_ring), border addition and stripping (br_add_border, br_strip_border,
br_inner_n), outer ring queries (br_outer_color, br_is_uniform_outer), multi-ring color
collection (br_ring_colors), range query (br_max_ring), concentric bullseye detection
(br_is_nested), ring depth maps (br_depth_map), and targeted ring filling (br_fill_ring).

Key implementation note: between/3 in SWI-Prolog requires integer bounds. Expressions
like H-1 are compound terms, not integers, and must be evaluated with H1 is H-1 before
use in between(0, H1, R). This rule is enforced in br_ring_cells, br_depth_map, and
br_fill_ring. The maplist-with-partial-application pattern is avoided in br_add_border
because it would add an extra argument position; findall with member/2 is used instead.

Test results: 42/42 PLUnit tests pass.

SPARC documentation updates in this release:
    Specification v132: Part 157, requirements BR-BR-001 through BR-BR-014.
    Pseudocode v125: Part 157, pseudocode for all 14 predicates.
    Architecture v126: ARCH-133, border pack design notes.
    Refinement v180: acceptance criteria AC-BR-001 through AC-BR-042.
    Completion v183: this release record.
    Tutorial: Chapter 128 added to all tutorial files.

Key design decisions:
  - xf_same_cells and xf_is_recolor use shared-variable clauses for zero-overhead
    cell comparison: Prolog unification guarantees structural identity
  - xf_d4 normalizes, applies op, then translates back to original top-left so the
    transformation preserves the object's position anchor
  - xf_any_d4 uses member+cut to return the first matching op deterministically;
    since id is first in the list, identity transforms are found immediately
  - xf_merge uses sort/2 which both sorts and deduplicates, handling overlapping
    cell sets correctly without explicit set-difference logic
  - xf_cell_d4_ is defined locally (not imported from pair pack) to keep xform
    self-contained; the formulas are identical


WORK PACKAGE 173: QUERY PACK (qu_*, Layer 152)
Branch: feature/wp173-query
PR: 258
Status: Complete

Deliverables:
  packs/query/pack.pl
  packs/query/prolog/query.pl   (14 qu_* predicates, 2 private helpers)
  packs/query/test/test_query.pl (42 PLUnit tests, 3 per predicate)

SPARC updates:
  Specification v138:    Part 163 added (QU-QU-001 through QU-QU-014)
  Pseudocode v131:       Part 163 pseudocode added
  Architecture v132:     ARCH-139 added
  Refinement v186:       AC-QU-001 through AC-QU-042 added
  Completion v189:       this record

Tutorial Chapter 134 (Ch134_Query.txt) added.
README.md updated to 173 work packages.
CLAUDE.md updated to current SPARC versions.

Key design decisions:
  - "Form" is defined as origin-normalized cell list (exact structural match), not
    D4-invariant. This keeps the query pack self-contained without importing D4
    machinery from the pair pack. Two L-shaped objects at different orientations have
    different forms.
  - Two-phase count pattern (findall distinct keys -> sort -> findall count per key)
    avoids all dynamic state and produces sorted output as a natural consequence.
  - Tie-breaking for most/least frequent color uses the sort order of the Color-N
    list (sorted by color); member+cut returns the smallest color at the target count.
  - Tie-breaking for largest/smallest obj preserves input order via findall (which
    collects in argument order); member+cut returns the first occurrence.
  - Uniformity tests use sort/2 -> singleton [_] pattern: concise and idiomatic.
  - qu_avg_size uses // (integer division) for floor average, consistent with the
    approach used in the arrange pack's centroid computation.


WORK PACKAGE 174: SIFT PACK (si_*, Layer 153)
Branch: feature/wp174-sift
PR: 259
Status: Complete

Deliverables:
  packs/sift/pack.pl
  packs/sift/prolog/sift.pl   (14 si_* predicates, 2 private helpers)
  packs/sift/test/test_sift.pl (42 PLUnit tests, 3 per predicate)

SPARC updates:
  Specification v139:    Part 164 added (SI-SI-001 through SI-SI-014)
  Pseudocode v132:       Part 164 pseudocode added
  Architecture v133:     ARCH-140 added
  Refinement v187:       AC-SI-001 through AC-SI-042 added
  Completion v190:       this record

Tutorial Chapter 135 (Ch135_Sift.txt) added.
README.md updated to 174 work packages.
CLAUDE.md updated to current SPARC versions.

Key design decisions:
  - All predicates use findall for filtering — uniform pattern, deterministic, preserves
    input order
  - si_max_size and si_min_size return ALL tied objects, unlike qu_largest_obj (which
    returns only the first). This is correct semantics for filtering: the caller wants
    "all the biggest ones", not "the first big one"
  - si_by_form and si_unique_color/si_shared_color are self-contained: normalization and
    color counting are implemented locally rather than importing from query or pair packs
  - si_on_border_ uses four clauses with cuts for deterministic border testing; unused
    head arguments in the R=:=0 and C=:=0 clauses are named _H, _W to suppress
    singleton warnings
  - si_off_border uses \+ (...member... si_on_border_): negation-as-failure over the
    existential "any cell on border" test


WORK PACKAGE 175: PIGMENT PACK (pg_*, Layer 154)
Branch: feature/wp175-pigment
PR: 260
Status: Complete

Deliverables:
  packs/pigment/pack.pl
  packs/pigment/prolog/pigment.pl   (14 pg_* predicates, 1 private helper)
  packs/pigment/test/test_pigment.pl (42 PLUnit tests, 3 per predicate)

SPARC updates:
  Specification v140:    Part 165 added (PG-PG-001 through PG-PG-014)
  Pseudocode v133:       Part 165 pseudocode added
  Architecture v134:     ARCH-141 added
  Refinement v188:       AC-PG-001 through AC-PG-042 added
  Completion v191:       this record

Tutorial Chapter 136 (Ch136_Pigment.txt) added.
README.md updated to 175 work packages.
CLAUDE.md updated to current SPARC versions.

Key design decisions:
  - if-then-else inside findall is the central pattern for conditional recoloring;
    idiomatic in SWI-Prolog and avoids accumulator-based recursion
  - pg_apply_table (lenient) vs pg_apply_table_strict: two distinct behaviors for
    the "apply rule" use case - the lenient form preserves all objects; strict form
    acts as a combined filter+transform
  - pg_infer_table matches by identical cell sets (same position, same cells), not
    D4-equivalent shapes; appropriate for inferring color maps between scenes where
    objects stay in place
  - pg_zip_recolor uses recursive three-clause form with cuts on both base cases to
    avoid choicepoints when one list ends before the other
  - pg_count_by_color_ is a private helper shared by all four frequency-targeted
    predicates; encapsulates the two-phase findall+sort count pattern
  - pg_consistent uses \+ with member+\=/2: negation-as-failure over the
    contradiction predicate "two entries with same From but different To"

predicates (is_added_only, is_removed_only, is_recolor_only, is_stable), and
a composite dl_scene_diff/3 that returns all components as a delta/4 term.
Enables multi-step ARC-AGI-2 reasoning by making "what transformation was
applied?" an answerable question.

Tests: 42/42 pass, no warnings.

Description: Partitions object scene lists into Key-[Objs] groups sharing a
common property. Partition predicates cover color, cell count (size), top row,
leftmost column, and origin-normalized form (shape). Inspection predicates
query group count, cardinalities, keys, and extrema. Filter predicates select
singleton or shared groups. gp_flatten reconstructs the flat object list.
gp_all_same_size tests uniform group cardinality. Determinism achieved via
cut and memberchk in extrema predicates. gp_by_form uses private gp_norm_
helper (same normalization algorithm as query and sift packs).

Three color-assignment predicates (by row, by col, by reading order) mirror the pattern of sizeop.sz_assign_colors but for spatial position. Four threshold predicates (above_row, from_row, left_of, from_col) and two band predicates (in_row_band, in_col_band) for positional set selection. All sorts use keysort/2 (stable) so equal-position objects preserve input order.

WP-184 Completion Record

Work Package: 184
Pack: objxf

Prefix: ox_
Layer: 163
Branch: feature/wp184-objxf-pack

Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): ox_bbox/5, ox_size/3, ox_translate/4, ox_to_origin/2, ox_recolor/3, ox_rot90/2, ox_rot180/2, ox_rot270/2, ox_reflect_h/2, ox_reflect_v/2, ox_merge/3, ox_diff/3, ox_intersect/3, ox_scale_up/3.

Tests: 60 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v149, Pseudo v142, Arch v143, Refinement v197, Completion v200.

Summary: Spatial and color transformations of obj(Color, Cells) terms. First pack to treat obj terms as geometric objects. Rotation formula: 90 CW maps r(R,C) -> r(R0+Lc, C0+(H-1)-Lr) using local coords (Lr=R-R0, Lc=C-C0). 180 maps r(R,C) -> r(R0+R1-R, C0+C1-C). 270 maps r(R,C) -> r(R0+(W-1)-Lc, C0+Lr). Reflect-h: r(R,C)->r(R0+R1-R,C). Reflect-v: r(R,C)->r(R,C0+C1-C). All use bounding-box-relative coordinates so result stays in same grid region. Scale-up uses between/3 to generate Factor x Factor block per cell. Set algebra: merge=append+sort; diff=findall with \+ member; intersect=findall with member.

WP-185 Completion Record

Work Package: 185
Pack: shrink
Module: shrink
Prefix: dn_
Layer: 164
Branch: feature/wp185-shrink-pack
PR: 270
Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): dn_block_dims/4, dn_block_cells/4, dn_block_color/5, dn_block_majority/5, dn_is_blocky/2, dn_shrink/3, dn_shrink_strict/3, dn_find_scale/2, dn_obj_shrink/3, dn_scale_factor/3, dn_uniform_blocks/3, dn_mixed_blocks/3, dn_block_grid/5, dn_block_val/5.

Tests: 52 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v150, Pseudo v143, Arch v144, Refinement v198, Completion v201.

Summary: Grid downscaling and NxN block decomposition. The inverse of ox_scale_up in objxf. A grid is N-blocky when every NxN partition tile is a uniform color. dn_block_dims gives the count of complete NxN blocks. dn_block_cells generates the r(R,C) coordinate set for one block. dn_block_color checks uniformity (fails on mixed blocks). dn_block_majority uses msort+last to find the dominant value. dn_is_blocky uses forall over all block indices. dn_shrink builds a smaller grid by majority vote per block; dn_shrink_strict requires all blocks to be uniform. dn_find_scale searches divisors from 2 upward. dn_obj_shrink divides every cell coordinate by N and deduplicates. dn_scale_factor searches N from 2 to 30 comparing normalized cell sets. dn_uniform_blocks and dn_mixed_blocks enumerate block types. dn_block_grid extracts an NxN sub-grid; dn_block_val returns a flat value list.

WP-186 Completion Record

Work Package: 186
Pack: objmorph
Module: objmorph
Prefix: om_
Layer: 165
Branch: feature/wp186-objmorph-pack
PR: 271
Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): om_neighbors4/2, om_neighbors8/2, om_boundary4/2, om_interior4/2, om_boundary8/2, om_interior8/2, om_dilate4/2, om_erode4/2, om_dilate8/2, om_erode8/2, om_dilate4_n/3, om_erode4_n/3, om_open4/2, om_close4/2.

Tests: 46 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v151, Pseudo v144, Arch v145, Refinement v199, Completion v202.

Summary: Morphological operations directly on obj(Color, Cells) terms without requiring a grid. Two neighborhood generators: om_neighbors4 (4 orthogonal neighbors) and om_neighbors8 (8 directional neighbors including diagonals). Boundary extraction: om_boundary4 keeps cells with at least one 4-neighbor outside the set; om_boundary8 uses 8-connectivity. Interior extraction: om_interior4 keeps cells where all 4 neighbors are inside; om_interior8 uses all 8 neighbors (stricter). Dilation: om_dilate4 and om_dilate8 expand by one step; implemented via findall over neighbor lists then append+sort union. Erosion: om_erode4 delegates to om_interior4; om_erode8 delegates to om_interior8. Iterated forms: om_dilate4_n and om_erode4_n recurse with N countdown. Compound operations: om_open4 = erode4 then dilate4 (removes thin protrusions); om_close4 = dilate4 then erode4 (fills small gaps). Key implementation: boundary uses \+ forall(member(N,Nbrs), member(N,S)); interior uses forall(member(N,Nbrs), member(N,S)).

WP-187 Completion Record

Work Package: 187
Pack: voronoi
Module: voronoi
Prefix: vn_
Layer: 166
Branch: feature/wp187-voronoi-pack
PR: 272
Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): vn_non_bg_cells/3, vn_non_bg_colors/3, vn_nearest_dist/5, vn_nearest_color/5, vn_paint_bg/3, vn_dist_map/3, vn_region_cells/4, vn_regions/3, vn_max_dist/3, vn_at_dist/4, vn_within_dist/4, vn_medial/3, vn_expand1/4, vn_expand_n/5.

Tests: 49 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v152, Pseudo v145, Arch v146, Refinement v200, Completion v203.

Summary: Nearest-color painting and Voronoi partitioning for 2D grids. Distinguishes background cells from non-background cells using a caller-supplied Bg value. Source queries: vn_non_bg_cells and vn_non_bg_colors collect sources from the grid. Nearest queries: vn_nearest_dist (min of findall Manhattan distances) and vn_nearest_color (sort D-V pairs, take first). Painting: vn_paint_bg maps each Bg cell to its nearest color; leaves non-Bg unchanged. Distance transform: vn_dist_map returns 0 for non-Bg cells, Manhattan distance for Bg cells. Voronoi regions: vn_region_cells and vn_regions partition Bg cells by their nearest color. Distance queries: vn_max_dist, vn_at_dist, vn_within_dist. Medial axis: vn_medial finds Bg cells equidistant from 2+ distinct colors by collecting all colors that achieve the minimum distance and requiring at least a 2-element sorted list. Expansion: vn_expand1 finds Bg cells 4-adjacent to a specific color; vn_expand_n uses Manhattan distance cutoff N.

WP-189 Completion Record

Work Package: 189
Pack: wavefront
Module: wavefront
Prefix: wf_
Layer: 168
Branch: feature/wp189-wavefront-pack
PR: 274
Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): wf_passable/3, wf_bfs/4, wf_reachable/4, wf_unreachable/4, wf_at_dist/3, wf_within_dist/3, wf_dist_of/3, wf_max_dist/2, wf_all_dists/2, wf_path_exists/4, wf_paint_bg/5, wf_multi_wave/4, wf_collision/4, wf_enclosed/3.

Tests: 41 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v154, Pseudo v147, Arch v148, Refinement v202, Completion v205.

Summary: BFS wavefront propagation from seed cells through passable cells in a 2D grid. Seeds enter the BFS at distance 0 regardless of their own color; the wave expands through 4-adjacent cells matching PassColor. The BFS worker (wf_bfs_) maintains an Enqueued set rather than a Visited set, adding new neighbors to both the queue and Enqueued immediately upon discovery to prevent duplicate insertions. wf_reachable returns all cells in the BFS tree; wf_unreachable returns PassColor cells absent from the tree. Distance queries (wf_at_dist, wf_within_dist, wf_dist_of, wf_max_dist, wf_all_dists) operate on the precomputed DistPairs list. wf_path_exists uses memberchk on a single BFS to avoid choicepoints. wf_paint_bg replaces each passable cell with min(BFS_distance, MaxD). wf_multi_wave and wf_collision pre-compute one BFS per color then scan passable cells: multi_wave assigns the winning color (minimum distance, ties by term order); collision collects cells where the minimum distance is achieved by 2+ colors. wf_enclosed seeds from all PassColor cells on the grid border and returns PassColor cells not reached.

WP-190 Completion Record

Work Package: 190
Pack: objchain
Module: objchain
Prefix: ch_
Layer: 169
Branch: feature/wp190-objchain-pack
PR: 275
Merged: 2026-06-26

Predicates (14): ch_touches/2, ch_degree/3, ch_is_chain/1, ch_has_cycle/1, ch_endpoints/3, ch_linearize/2, ch_from_endpoint/3, ch_nth/3, ch_color_seq/2, ch_sub/4, ch_reverse/2, ch_length/2, ch_is_linear_path/1, ch_direction/2.

Tests: 48 PLUnit tests, all pass, no warnings.

SPARC: Spec v155, Pseudo v148, Arch v149, Refinement v203, Completion v206.

Summary: Linear chain detection and traversal for obj(Color, Cells) collections. A chain is a connected set of objects whose touching graph is a simple path. ch_touches checks 4-adjacency (same row/col, distance 1; cut after first pair). ch_degree counts touching neighbors within Objs. ch_is_chain detects a path via degree constraints: no degree > 2, no degree 0, exactly two degree-1 objects (endpoints). ch_has_cycle detects a closed cycle: N >= 3 and all degrees = 2 (using =\= for arithmetic inequality). ch_walk_ traverses the chain DFS-style: at each step finds the unique unvisited touching neighbor (using ch_next_); stops when no neighbor remains. ch_linearize calls ch_endpoints then ch_walk_. ch_from_endpoint starts from a caller-specified object. ch_direction checks if min-row uniform (h), min-col uniform (v), or neither (other); uses forall/2 with R =:= R0. ch_is_linear_path verifies an ordered sequence recursively (O1 touches O2; recurse on tail). Fixed: ch_has_cycle used invalid `\=:=`; corrected to `=\=` (SWI-Prolog arithmetic not-equal).

WP-196: objseq Pack — Object Sequence and Progression Analysis

Status: Complete.
Layer: 175.
Prefix: oq_*.
Exports: 14 predicates.
Tests: 41/41 pass.

Description: Analyses ordered sequences of obj(Color, Cells) terms for
patterns in color, size, and spatial position. Detects growing/shrinking
size progressions, equal centroid spacing, periodic color and size cycles,
collinear centroid arrangements, and predicts the next position in a regular
spatial sequence. Companion pack to arrange (spatial ordering) and query
(aggregate statistics).

Evidence: packs/objseq/prolog/objseq.pl, packs/objseq/test/test_objseq.pl.
Documentation: Spec v161 Part 186, Pseudo v154 Part 186, Arch v155 ARCH-162,
Refinement v209 AC-OQ-001 through AC-OQ-041.


WP-197: objdelta Pack — Object-Pair Change Analysis and Rule Application

Status: Complete.
Layer: 176.
Prefix: dp_*.
Exports: 14 predicates.
Tests: 41/41 pass.

Description: Analyses O1-O2 pairs of obj(Color, Cells) terms to extract what
changed between before and after: colour, centroid displacement, or cell
count. Extracts generalised colour maps from a list of pairs and applies them
to new objects. Tests form equality and positional equality. Computes cell-
level intersection and symmetric difference.

Evidence: packs/objdelta/prolog/objdelta.pl, packs/objdelta/test/test_objdelta.pl.
Documentation: Spec v162 Part 187, Pseudo v155 Part 187, Arch v156 ARCH-163,
Refinement v210 AC-DP-001 through AC-DP-041.

Status: Complete.
Layer: 177.
Prefix: tc_*.
Exports: 14 predicates.
Tests: 41/41 pass.

Description: Generates multiple copies of obj(Color, Cells) terms at computed
positions. Provides explicit placement by top-left corner, tiling in rows,
columns, and grids, aligning and packing lists of objs, spreading at fixed
column/row intervals, centering within a canvas, and canvas-frame horizontal
reflection.

ARC-AGI-2 Benchmark: Wave 3 — arm_endpoint_ray (Acc_301, 2026-06-27)
Status: COMPLETE
Score: 3 / 120 = 2.50%
Task solved: 80a900e0
Rule: arm_endpoint_ray — checkerboard background of alternating 0s and 1s
contains diagonal arm segments. Each arm endpoint (a non-bg cell with
exactly one same-color diagonal neighbor in one direction and zero in the
other) shoots a perpendicular ray through background-1 cells, recoloring
them with the arm color. Rays stop at grid boundaries or non-bg cells.
Junction cells (same-color neighbors in both diagonal directions) and
midpoints (two neighbors in the same direction) are excluded by the
structural test.
New predicates: arc2_replace_idx_/4, arc2_set_cell_/5,
arc2_diag_nbr_cnt_/6, arc2_arm_endpoints_/2, arc2_shoot_ray_/9,

ARC-AGI-2 Benchmark: Wave 4 — segment_equalize (Acc_302, 2026-06-27)
Status: COMPLETE
Score: 4 / 120 = 3.33%
Task solved: e376de54
Rule: segment_equalize — non-background cells form linear segments in one
direction (horizontal, vertical, or anti-diagonal). One endpoint of every
segment is aligned to a common value (the anchor); the other is extended or
trimmed to match the middle segment by sorted position. For anti-diagonal
segments the alignment value is r-c of the endpoint cell (2*row - key),
enabling direction-invariant equalization. The correct non-anchor endpoint
for key K and target alignment D is row = (K+D)//2 (anti-diagonal) or the
alignment value directly (horizontal/vertical).
New predicates: arc2_segeq_kv_/5, arc2_segeq_align_/4,
arc2_segeq_cvary_/4, arc2_segeq_cellpos_/5, arc2_segeq_consec_/1,
arc2_segeq_dir_/2, arc2_segeq_build_segs_/3, arc2_segeq_anchor_/4,
arc2_segeq_setrange_/7, arc2_segeq_adj1_/7, arc2_segeq_adjall_/7.

ARC-AGI-2 Benchmark: Wave 5 - stub_rank_fill (Acc_303, 2026-06-27)
Status: COMPLETE
Score: 5 / 120 = 4.17%
Task solved: 97d7923e
Rule: stub_rank_fill - column stubs at the top of the grid rank which vertical
bar to fill. A stub of length N at column C with color V means "select the
Nth-largest vertical bar with endpoint color V (by body length, descending) and
fill its body with V." A vertical bar has pattern [V, B, ..., B, V] in a single
column where V is the endpoint color and B is the body color. Body cells (between
the two endpoints) are replaced with V for the selected bar. Multiple stubs are
processed independently in a single pass.
New predicates: arc2_srf_top_run_/5, arc2_srf_find_vbar_/8,
arc2_srf_apply_fills_/3, arc2_srf_in_fill_zone_/4.

ARC-AGI-2 Benchmark: Wave 6 - band_wrap (Acc_304, 2026-06-27)
Status: COMPLETE
Score: 6 / 120 = 5.00%
Task solved: 45a5af55
Rule: band_wrap - the input consists of uniform solid-color rows (each row is one
solid color). The row-color sequence is run-length encoded into (Color, Count) bands.
The output is a square grid of side S = 2*TotalCount - LastCount, where TotalCount
is the sum of all band counts and LastCount is the count of the final band. Each
output cell (R,C) is assigned the color of the band whose cumulative count bracket
contains the ring index min(R, C, S-1-R, S-1-C). The first band fills the outermost
ring, the last band fills the center square, and intermediate bands fill concentric
rectangular rings of thickness equal to their count.
New predicates: arc2_bw_uniform_/2, arc2_bw_rle_rows_/2, arc2_bw_rle_same_/5,
arc2_bw_sum_counts_/2, arc2_bw_ring_color_/3.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
PR: Mentova #315 (pending)
SPARC: Specification v240, Pseudocode v232, Architecture v235, Refinement v287, Completion v293


ARC-AGI-2 WAVE 7 COMPLETION RECORD

Date: 2026-06-27
Score: 7 / 120 = 5.83%
Task solved: 4c3d4a41
Rule: staircase_lift - the 8x20 grid is divided into a left half (cols 0-8) encoding
a staircase of 5-values at odd columns 1,3,5,7, and a right half (cols 9-19) with a
rectangular frame and four vertical color bars at odd columns 11,13,15,17. For each
bar i, the staircase height H[i] in left odd column (2i+1) determines the maximum
output row: MaxEnd = 5 - H[i]. The color bar is placed flush to that row with its
height clipped to fit: OutHeight = min(InputLength, MaxEnd), OutEnd = MaxEnd,
OutStart = OutEnd - OutHeight + 1. The left half is cleared to 0 in the output;
the right-half frame is preserved; rows below OutEnd in each bar column are 5
(staircase fill); row 5 inner bar at cols 11-17 becomes all 5.
New predicates: arc2_sl_col_h_/3, arc2_sl_count_up_/5, arc2_sl_bar_/4,
arc2_sl_first_color_/5, arc2_sl_run_len_/5, arc2_sl_out_/4, arc2_sl_val_/4.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 9: panel_overlay - Four-panel flood-fill boundary rule (task 7491f3cf).
The input grid has four 5x5 panels. Panel 1 defines a wall (main 8-connected
component) plus a seed (isolated extra cell). A 4-connected flood fill from the
seed labels cells as L-region (s2 side) or R-region (s3 side). Panel 4 is filled:
L-region = s2, R-region = s3, wall = s2 if non-bg else s3.
New predicates: arc2_po_panels_/2, arc2_po_slice_/4, arc2_po_flat3_/4,
arc2_po_nonbg_pos_/3, arc2_po_seed_/2, arc2_po_flood4_/3, arc2_po_bfs4_/4,
arc2_po_build_result_/8, arc2_po_cell_val_/8.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
SPARC: Specification v241, Pseudocode v233, Architecture v236, Refinement v290, Completion v296

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 10: apex_shadow - Arm-vector shadow projection rule (task 409aa875).
Each shape's centre (apex of a chevron or corner of an L-shape) projects a shadow
via its two arm vectors.  Projection = -(arm1+arm2)*5/max(|sR|,|sC|).  Background
target gets 9; two projections to same bg cell get 1 (collision); non-bg target
triggers component recolour to 9.  Covers four chevron orientations and four
L-shape orientations uniformly with no special cases.  Key fix: replaced the
incorrect global-leftmost-column offset with per-shape arm-vector normalisation.
New predicates: as_comp_proj_/7, as_arm_proj_/10, as_8nbr_wings_/5,
as_bg_nonbg_split_/5, as_count_hits_/2.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
SPARC: Specification v241, Pseudocode v233, Architecture v236, Refinement v291, Completion v297

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 11: sym_restore - Per-colour vertical symmetry restoration (task 8e5c0c38).
Each non-background colour group has a vertical mirror axis (integer or half-integer
column).  For each group the rule finds the axis that minimises the number of orphan
cells (cells whose column-mirror is absent from the group), then removes those orphans
by setting them to background.  Train 0 (bg=8): colour 1 axis=8.0 removes 3 orphans,
colour 2 axis=13.0 removes 3 orphans, colour 6 axis=17.0 removes 1 orphan.  Train 1
(bg=0): colour 2 axis=16.5 removes 2 orphans, colour 4 axis=12.0 removes 2 orphans,
colour 8 axis=7.0 removes 2 orphans.  Test (bg=1): colour 3 axis=18.0 removes 2,
colour 4 axis=6.0 removes 3, colour 6 axis=9.5 removes 12; total 17 changes.
New predicates: sr_color_groups_/3, sr_all_orphans_/2, sr_best_v_orphans_/2,
sr_min_orphans_/3, sr_orphans_for_axis_/3, sr_remove_rows_/5, sr_remove_row_/6.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
SPARC: Specification v241, Pseudocode v233, Architecture v236, Refinement v292, Completion v298

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 12: waterfall - Gravity-based 6-flow around obstacles (task 36a08778).
Existing 6-seed cells flow downward by gravity through background cells.  When a 6-cell
is blocked below by an in-grid obstacle (non-bg, non-6), it spreads horizontally in its
current row in both directions.  Spreading stops at the first cell that CAN drain down
(included in the fill range, drain point) or at a barrier (existing 6, obstacle, or grid
boundary).  OOB below does NOT trigger spreading; the 6 simply halts at the bottom.  The
result is a connected network of 6-filled paths outlining each obstacle cluster and linking
back to the original seeds, exactly matching the training examples.  All 6 training pairs
and the test case of task 36a08778 pass.  Score advance: 11/120 = 9.17% to 12/120 = 10.00%.
New predicates: wf_bfs_/7, wf_eff_/6, wf_spread_/9, wf_edge_/10, wf_enq_/5,

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 13: odd_col - Unique col section extraction per row section (task 38007db0).
The grid is a tiling of identical-sized rectangular cells separated by uniform separator
rows and cols.  One col section per row section has a unique interior pattern differing
from all the other col sections in that row.  The output collapses the grid to one col
section wide by extracting the unique col section for each row section.  Identification
uses majority voting across content rows: for each content row, the strip that differs
from the majority strip casts a vote; the col section with the most votes is the unique
one.  Both training pairs and the test case of task 38007db0 pass.
Score advance: 12/120 = 10.00% to 13/120 = 10.83%.
New predicates: oc_all_same_/2, oc_adjacent_pairs_/2, oc_strip_/4,
oc_strips_for_row_/4, oc_majority_strip_/2, oc_find_unique_idx_/3,
oc_vote_unique_col_/5, oc_build_secs_/5.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 14: reflect_axis - Shape reflection across 2-marker axis (task 7ed72f31).
Each non-background non-2 shape is paired with its nearest cluster of 2-cells. The axis
type is determined by the cluster geometry: a single 2-cell gives a 180-degree point
reflection; a collinear column of 2-cells gives a vertical axis; a collinear row of
2-cells gives a horizontal axis. The original shapes and 2-markers are preserved;
reflected copies are added. Both training pairs (bg=1 with 4 shapes; bg=8 with 3 shapes)
and the test case of task 7ed72f31 pass.
Score advance: 13/120 = 10.83% to 14/120 = 11.67%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 15: period_repair - Periodic-pattern deviation repair (task 135a2760).
Finds inner sequences between wall markers. For each sequence, selects period P with
minimum residue-class support >= 0.75 and fewest errors (1..3); repairs deviating cells.
Row repair first, then column repair via transpose-repair-transpose. A cut-free induction
guard uses once/1 to commit to the first wall marker without cutting fallback clauses.
The periodic_repair induction yields to period_repair when period_repair also solves
all training pairs, preventing priority conflicts between similar rules.
New predicates: pr2_repair_row_/3, pr2_fix_segs_/3, pr2_extract_/4, pr2_apply_fixes_/4,
pr2_replace_nth0_/4, pr2_best_period_/4, pr2_majority_base_/3, pr2_min_support_/4,
pr2_errors_/4, pr2_mode_/2, pr2_mode_acc_/6.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 16: legend_fill - Frame-interior fill from color lookup table (task dbff022c).
Detects a compact legend table (solid 2xN or Nx2 block of non-identical non-background rows
or columns) embedded in the grid. Key direction determined by which legend row or column
contains more frame-border colors (colors that enclose background cells via flood fill from
the grid boundary). For each key color K: enclosed background cells whose only non-background
neighbors are K are filled with the corresponding value V from the legend.
Two key implementation lessons:
  (1) Find the LONGEST solid block (not leftmost). Use findall over all starting positions
      then max_member; the leftmost solid run can be shorter than a later, longer legend.
  (2) Require the two legend rows or columns to be non-identical; this filters uniform
      frame-border segments (e.g., [2,2]/[2,2]) from being mistaken for the legend.
New predicates: lf_legend_/4, lf_best_block_/4, lf_row_block_/5, lf_col_block_/5,
  lf_solid_run_/7, lf_solid_end_/6, lf_orient_kv_/6, lf_enclosed_all_/3, lf_flood_/7,
  lf_frame_colors_/4, lf_apply_fill_/5, lf_enclosed_for_color_/4,
  lf_unique_frame_color_/5, lf_fill_grid_/4, lf_take_/4, lf_extract_col_/3.
Also added imports: max_member/2 from library(lists), foldl/4 and maplist/4 from
  library(apply), pairs_keys_values/3 from library(pairs).

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 17: frame_target legend-direction rule (2026-06-28)
Added arc2_named_rule(frame_target), arc2_induce_rule/2 clause, arc2_transform/3 clause,
and helper predicates (ft_* prefix) to arc_benchmark_2.pl. The frame_target rule identifies
small legend rectangles (border = color C, dense interior with 2-marker cells) and derives
a movement direction (Dr, Dc) from the 2-cell centroid relative to the interior center. Each
dot-4 enclosed within the large irregular frame of the same color C is advanced step by step
in direction (Dr, Dc) until one step before the nearest C-colored wall, using a three-way
diagonal clip test. Task solved: 88e364bc. Score: 17/120 = 14.17%.

actual Color_ positions; added 10-second per-task limit via call_with_time_limit/2; removed
pair-induction from the benchmark loop (reduces full run from timeout to ~2 minutes).

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 18: tip_escape release note (2026-06-28)
Added arc2_named_rule(tip_escape), arc2_transform(tip_escape,...),
arc2_induce_rule([...], tip_escape) and helper predicates (te_* prefix)
to arc_benchmark_2.pl. The tip_escape rule identifies shape components
(8-connected non-background regions) and their enclosed marker components
(different color, smaller, bounding box inside shape bounding box), finds
the shape's tip (unique single cell at an extreme row/col), and places
min(N_markers, dist_to_edge) marker cells just past the tip in the escape
direction. Escape direction chosen by apex detection (perpendicular diverging
shape-cell arms at tip) or, if no apex, by projection method
(escape_vector = shape_centroid - marker_centroid; pick tip with max projection).

Wave 28 - slide_open (WP-286, Layer 261):
  Task: 6e453dd6.
  Score: 27/120 = 22.50% -> 28/120 = 23.33%.
  Rule name: slide_open.
  Rule: Find the vertical 5-divider column DC. Partition all 0-cells left
  of DC into 4-connected components. Slide each component right so its
  rightmost cell touches column DC-1. After sliding, for each row where
  cell(DC-1)=0 AND cell(DC-2)!=0 AND a 0-cell exists in columns 0..DC-3,
  fill columns DC+1..NCols-1 with value 2.
  Mentova PR merged. PrologAI PR linked.

Wave 29 - diag_beam (WP-287, Layer 262):
  Task: db695cfb.
  Score: 28/120 = 23.33% -> 29/120 = 24.17%.
  Rule name: diag_beam.
  Rule: Guard verifies all non-BG cells are 1 or 6. Find all unordered
  pairs of 1-cells where |row_diff| = |col_diff| > 0 (diagonal alignment).
  For each pair, march a beam from one 1 toward the other along the 45-degree
  diagonal: fill background cells with 1; when a 6-obstacle is hit, leave
  it unchanged and fire two perpendicular rays from it, each filling
  background cells with 6 until the grid boundary or another existing 6.
  Mentova PR merged. PrologAI PR linked.
  SPARC updated: Specification v258, Pseudocode v250, Architecture v251,
  Refinement v310, Completion v316.

Wave 30 - frame_absorb (WP-288, Layer 263):
  Task: d35bdbdc.
  Score: 29/120 = 24.17% -> 30/120 = 25.00%.
  Rule name: frame_absorb.
  Rule: Identify frame blocks (3x3 squares or cross shapes) by 4-connected
  component analysis, excluding background (0) and snake (5) cells. Each
  block has CV (center color) and AV (arm color). Build absorption graph:
  X.CV = Y.AV means X absorbs Y. Process monochrome blocks (CV=AV) first,
  then chain starts (no predecessor), then cycle fallback (erase all).
  Absorbing: Y's cells set to 0, X's center repainted with Y.CV.
  Mentova PR #343 merged. PrologAI PR linked.
  SPARC updated: Specification v260, Pseudocode v252, Architecture v253,
  Refinement v312, Completion v318.

Wave 37 complete: concentric_rings (WP-295, Layer 270).
Task: 13e47133.
Score: 36/120 = 30.00% -> 37/120 = 30.83%.
Rule name: concentric_rings.
Rule: BG (most frequent) and Div (most frequent non-BG) partition non-Div cells
  into 4-connected components via flood-fill. Each component fills with
  concentric rectangular rings: ring-0 = grid boundary or 8-adjacent to any Div
  cell; ring K = BFS distance K from ring-0 sources (4-connected). Single-cell
  non-BG non-Div markers define the color cycle per component; cycle repeats.
  8-connected Div-adjacency for ring-0 handles L-shaped components where Div
  corner cells mark concavity boundary cells via diagonal adjacency.
Mentova PR merged. PrologAI PR linked.

WAVE 39: room_outline (WP-297, Layer 272) — 2026-07-01
Task 8f3a5a89 solved. Score: 36/120 = 30.00% -> 37/120 = 30.83%.
Rule name: room_outline.
Key insight: perimeter generation requires boundary-connected walls. Wall
components not attached to the grid boundary are floating islands that do not
create perimeter cells. Two-phase component algorithm: (1) WallKeep = components
touching the accessible region; (2) BdryWalls = WallKeep components that include
a grid-edge cell; perimeter cells are accessible BG cells on the grid edge or
8-adjacent to BdryWalls.

WAVE 40: grid_tile (WP-298, Layer 273) — 2026-07-01
Task eee78d87 solved. Score: 37/120 = 30.83% -> 38/120 = 31.67%.
Rule name: grid_tile.
Key insight: the 3x3 bounding box of the input's colored cells encodes a periodic
tiling via four named positions: corners->block, top/bottom midpoints->v_edge,
left/right midpoints->h_edge, center->corner. Each position maps to a specific
structural role in the period-3 background grid. The active region (rows 5-10,
cols 5-10 in the 16x16 output) replaces background-0 with 9, providing the
task's signature highlight pattern. The tiling and highlight are fully separable:
decode tile first, then build output in a single pass.
Mentova PR merged. PrologAI PR linked.

Wave 73 - lattice_stamp (WP-331, Layer 306, Acc_371)
Rule: lattice_stamp
Task: a395ee82
